<div id="review_947409226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947409226" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947409226?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947409226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6846707366370431170">This is beautifully written, as all of Patricia McKillip's work is. However, something in the density of it makes it difficult -- not to read; I sped through it, in that sense, but to understand exactly what it going on and how we should feel about it. I've had that problem with one or two of McKillip's other books, so I think it's something about her style which may or may not be a problem for other people. I wouldn't actually start here, with McKillip: I first fell in love with <i>The Changeling </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6846707366370431170" style="display:none">This is beautifully written, as all of Patricia McKillip's work is. However, something in the density of it makes it difficult -- not to read; I sped through it, in that sense, but to understand exactly what it going on and how we should feel about it. I've had that problem with one or two of McKillip's other books, so I think it's something about her style which may or may not be a problem for other people. I wouldn't actually start here, with McKillip: I first fell in love with <i>The Changeling Sea</i>, I think, and I'd start there if I could begin with her work again.<br /><br />Nonetheless, it is beautifully written and a joy to read in that sense. You might find yourself lingering over a sentence, a paragraph, because of the way it's put together.<br /><br />I can't help but think that Le Guin's Ged and McKillip's Morgon have a certain amount in common. They're both driven by their destinies, rather than following them willingly. They baulk more than a hero-type like, say, Aragorn or Frodo. Maybe slightly more in common with Bilbo, wishing he could be back home listening to his kettle sing, and Morgon especially shares that unwillingness and the sense that the goal is not really his own.<br /><br />I'm not entirely sure what I think of the world-building. There's a lot of fascinating stuff here, revealed in a careful way (avoiding any info dumps like "as you know, Bob, the wizards disappeared seven hundred years ago"). But the story is so clearly unfinished, so clearly part of a trilogy -- maybe not even a trilogy, I can't see how this could be a complete book on its own in any sense, it doesn't really come to any conclusion. So I'll reserve broader judgement for later. Onwards!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6846707366370431170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/10551293-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646268618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4345038297339825232">This is one of those border books that not everyone has heard of but is actually probably my favorite book ever. I have read it and reread it probably a hundred times and will reread it for comfort up there with Pride and Prejudice and Unbearable Lightness of Being-- all books I could read over and over without getting sick of them. For anyone who would look at this and dismiss it as stupid fantasy writing they are missing the huge parable that dies not make sense until you read the last chapter</span>
  <span id="freeText4345038297339825232" style="display:none">This is one of those border books that not everyone has heard of but is actually probably my favorite book ever. I have read it and reread it probably a hundred times and will reread it for comfort up there with Pride and Prejudice and Unbearable Lightness of Being-- all books I could read over and over without getting sick of them. For anyone who would look at this and dismiss it as stupid fantasy writing they are missing the huge parable that dies not make sense until you read the last chapter of the third book. For anyone who knows Patricia Mckillip's writing they will know what I mean. What is dark and evil is not always evil but ultimately good and vice versa. She creates a dualistic universe that you have to be patient for it to reveal itself. Morgan is a character who is born to one identity but realizes he is actually a legend that has been referred to by previous ridlemasters and wizards. The book is about his journey to find out the truth about this identity that is alluded to and how much of himself he is willing to lose or give away in the process. On one hand it is a simple fantasy story but it is rich enough for someone to see that it is a parable to all of us about how we define ourselves and what we are willing to sacrifice to keep believing in what may be shattered perceptions of who we really are.Morgan runs the gamut from naive to angry and dangerous to self sacrificing to become the ultimate weapon of good or evil...he doesnt know which.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4345038297339825232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17280997127267529817">I'll review this book a little different than usual. Reason being I had extremely high expectations regarding this. I love riddles, mazes, creepy castles, Celtic themed fantasy, with a deep and interesting lore. <br/><br/>The good: Awesome idea for a fantasy setting, decent world building, the idea of riddles being involved, interesting magic, quest, mysteries, riddle college, and Celtic themes. <br/><br/>The bad: weak characterization, insanely boring dialogue, slow chore like pace, no real riddles, and it's just </span>
  <span id="freeText17280997127267529817" style="display:none">I'll review this book a little different than usual. Reason being I had extremely high expectations regarding this. I love riddles, mazes, creepy castles, Celtic themed fantasy, with a deep and interesting lore. <br /><br />The good: Awesome idea for a fantasy setting, decent world building, the idea of riddles being involved, interesting magic, quest, mysteries, riddle college, and Celtic themes. <br /><br />The bad: weak characterization, insanely boring dialogue, slow chore like pace, no real riddles, and it's just plain boring. <br /><br />This book was extremely difficult to finish, I really wanted to like it. Sadly the characterization and dialogue is insanely boring and doesn't feel real at all. The book is short but reads like a chore, feels like it takes forever just go get through it. <br /><br />I was tempted to give it one star but decided against it for a couple reasons. It really is an interesting idea for a fantasy series, but sadly didn't deliver. Also, I can't give this book 1 star knowing insanely awfully crappy books like fifty shades of grey also got one star from me. No book deserves to be next to that price of garbage. <br /><br />This book didn't deliver the goods and is just plain boring. </span>

<div id="review_627433871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/627433871" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator" href="/user/show/20781309-anhec-the-paperback-obliterator">AnHeC the Paperback Obliterator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788387968502" href="/book/show/6184472-mistrz-zagadek-z-hed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20781309-anhec-the-paperback-obliterator?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer627433871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8181250314423131392">Now, I should start with admitting I'm partial to this book. I've read it as a kid, it was a gift from my parents (whole 3 books). And I loved it. It had some wisdom in it, that I needed at the time. And a few of my favourite quotes hit me still today.<br/><br/>So, let's get on with review.<br/><br/>I liked the main character. I liked the fact, that he didn't necessarily seek glory. Didn't want to save the world, so to speak. An unwilling hero. A guy that loves peace and quite and books (^^) but life has other idea</span>
  <span id="freeText8181250314423131392" style="display:none">Now, I should start with admitting I'm partial to this book. I've read it as a kid, it was a gift from my parents (whole 3 books). And I loved it. It had some wisdom in it, that I needed at the time. And a few of my favourite quotes hit me still today.<br /><br />So, let's get on with review.<br /><br />I liked the main character. I liked the fact, that he didn't necessarily seek glory. Didn't want to save the world, so to speak. An unwilling hero. A guy that loves peace and quite and books (^^) but life has other ideas.<br /><br /><br />I didn't like how riddles were presented. They weren't really riddles. It was just knowledge, at least seemed like it at parts. But even after all those years it still is a refreshing concept (or at least an interesting one).<br /><br />I also liked other characters. They were distinct, consistent, and often if not likeable than at least interesting or understandable. <br /><br />The book on it's own may not deserve 5 stars, but for me (with all the history and emotional attachment), that's what it's worth so that's what I gave. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8181250314423131392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3214723435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3214723435" />
    <a title="prcardi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi"><img alt="prcardi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471708128p2/43250213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3214723435?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prcardi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prcardi" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi">prcardi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345288813" href="/book/show/816991.The_Riddle_Master_of_Hed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=pg">pg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214723435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5967549072525165654">Storyline: 3/5<br/>Characters: 2/5<br/>Writing Style: 3/5<br/>World: 4/5<br/><br/><i>The Riddle-Master of Hed</i> was published a little late for getting away with the hurried pacing and thin characterization, but some of the components here are just so rich to give excuse to the many deviations from Great Book demands. It is easy to see how this would be a classic. It has several hallmarks of an epic: the eye-opening personal evolution, the quest, the introductions to powerful objects and great events. McKlllip adds to that b</span>
  <span id="freeText5967549072525165654" style="display:none">Storyline: 3/5<br />Characters: 2/5<br />Writing Style: 3/5<br />World: 4/5<br /><br /><i>The Riddle-Master of Hed</i> was published a little late for getting away with the hurried pacing and thin characterization, but some of the components here are just so rich to give excuse to the many deviations from Great Book demands. It is easy to see how this would be a classic. It has several hallmarks of an epic: the eye-opening personal evolution, the quest, the introductions to powerful objects and great events. McKlllip adds to that base an enigmatic world with questions unanswered. Generally, this is a bonus, giving a dose of mystique to what is otherwise an episodic adventure tale. In some places it does hamper the world and characters, as it is never clear that what is extraordinary to the reader is anything but ordinary to book characters. Ultimately what makes this a standout is the profession of the Riddle-Masters and the art involved with the harp. The former is simply excellent fantasy worldbuilding, changing the way readers think about matters that others coast through without thought. The latter binds artistry and wonder together in a way that gave an added flair to the tale. There are modern fantasies that are so much better at writing; they understand pacing, characterization, and plotting. But not all authors, present or past, manage <i>the idea</i>. Whenever someone does, as McKillip here, it is worth stopping and noticing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5967549072525165654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zUg6+WL+afqpip6ogvLNos8FPWT2oJPAieRYNsgPKejAueK5jsWwYS+eUM46CZSt8f78IXIakN55SLtzcWF7Lw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mwQTUMeEcmPKt6FUeaZKMvE/Ji/PXMw81MKpr3WoKM2W9csQK7+r+EyjbzLBXRM9z8TnakvmzyIkbkrqzMZ6Cg==')})
  }

In later legends, he was to become a figure of mystery, known as both the defender of humanity and the patron saint of dark magic. But now he sought only retirement on his family estates.\n\nHis dream of justice and amicable relations between the races had turned to ashes in his mind. The medieval kingdom of Gwynedd groaned under the tyranny of Imre and his sister and mistress, Ariella. Normal humans were savagely persecuted by the king, whose Deryni ancestors had seized the throne from the rightful human Haldane line a century before. Camber could not even save his own son from the murderous treachery of Imre.\n\nWhen Camber learned that Cinhil Haldane, a descendant of the previous kings, still lived, he realized that the only hope for the kingdom lay in overthrowing Imre and restoring Cinhil to the throne. But Cinhil was a cloistered monk, hidden under his religious name in one of many monasteries, unaware of his heritage, untrained in politics. Could he be persuaded to leave the only life he knew and take on the leadership of a rebellion? And lacking the Deryni powers, could he hope to overcome the magic of the king? \n\nGrimly, Camber set out to locate Cinhil and spirit him from the cloister into a struggle that seemed doomed from the start.\n\nAnd behind came the minions of the king—for Imre was already aware of the plot and bent on destroying all involved in it.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2492532948799619913\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25.Patricia_A_McKillip">About Patricia A. McKillip</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25.Patricia_A_McKillip"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1220752490p3/25.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25.Patricia_A_McKillip">Patricia A. McKillip
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,168
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7394230416160763455">Patricia Anne McKillip is an American author of fantasy and science fiction novels, distinguished by lyrical, delicate prose and careful attention to detail and characterization. She is a past winner of the World Fantasy Award and Locus Award, and she lives in Oregon. Most of her recent novels have cover paintings by Kinuko Y. Craft. She is married to David Lunde, a poet.<br/><br/>According to Fantasy Book </span>
  <span id="freeText7394230416160763455" style="display:none">Patricia Anne McKillip is an American author of fantasy and science fiction novels, distinguished by lyrical, delicate prose and careful attention to detail and characterization. She is a past winner of the World Fantasy Award and Locus Award, and she lives in Oregon. Most of her recent novels have cover paintings by Kinuko Y. Craft. She is married to David Lunde, a poet.<br /><br />According to Fantasy Book Review, Patricia McKillip grew up in Oregon, England, and Germany, and received a Bachelor of Arts (English) in 1971 and a Master of Arts in 1973 from San Jose State University.<br /><br />McKillip's stories usually take place in a setting similar to the Middle Ages. There are forests, castles, and lords or kings, minstrels, tinkers and wizards. Her writing usually puts her characters in situations involving mysterious powers that they don't understand. Many of her characters aren't even sure of their own ancestry. Music often plays an important role. Love between family members is also important in McKillip's writing, although members of her families often disagree.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7394230416160763455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
